Hi Kai,

I've had a chance to review the challenges you're facing with calibrating the volatility surface model. Here are my thoughts:

1. **Singular Covariance Matrix**: Consider incorporating additional market factors or using regularization methods for covariance. Employing Ledoit-Wolf shrinkage can help stabilize the matrix during stress periods.

2. **ATM Skew and Non-Linear Behavior**: You may need to introduce jump components into your model to accommodate outliers effectively. Jump diffusion models could capture the tail behavior better during times of market stress.

3. **Calibration Timing**: If you're currently using 5 years of minute-bar data, you might want to streamline this process or consider leveraging high-frequency data to gain faster calibrations while improving the robustness of your dataset.

4. **Overall Performance**: Given that real-time calibration for trading is crucial, consider utilizing machine learning algorithms to supplement existing calibration processes which might aid in achieving quicker and more precise forecasts.
